<p>The <b>Most Serene House of Braganza</b> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt"><i>Sereníssima Casa de Bragança</i></span>), or the <b>Brigantine Dynasty</b> (<i>Dinastia Brigantina</i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Dynasty" title="Dynasty">dynasty</a> of emperors, kings, princes, and dukes of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> origin, a branch of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Aviz" title="House of Aviz">House of Aviz</a>.</p>
<p>Founded by <a href="/wiki/Afonso_I,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Afonso I, Duke of Braganza">Afonso I, 1st Duke of Braganza</a>, illegitimate son of King <a href="/wiki/John_I_of_Portugal" title="John I of Portugal">John I of Portugal</a>, the Braganzas were one of the wealthiest and most powerful noble houses of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Renaissance" title="Portuguese Renaissance">Renaissance</a> period. The house came to rule the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Kingdom of Portugal</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Algarves" title="Kingdom of the Algarves">the Algarves</a> following the successful deposition of the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Dynasty" title="Philippine Dynasty">Philippine Dynasty</a> by <a href="/wiki/John_IV_of_Portugal" title="John IV of Portugal">John IV of Portugal</a>, in 1580. With the creation of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil_and_the_Algarves" title="United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves">United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves</a>, in 1815, and the subsequent independence of the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a>, in 1822, the Braganzas came to rule as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_Brazil" title="List of monarchs of Brazil">monarchs of Brazil</a>.</p>
<p>The House of Braganza produced 15 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Portuguese_monarchs" title="List of Portuguese monarchs">Portuguese monarchs</a> and 4 monarchs of Brazil, numerous consorts to various European kingdoms, such as <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Braganza" title="Catherine of Braganza">Catherine of Braganza</a> (wife of <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II of England</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Maria_Isabel_of_Braganza" title="Maria Isabel of Braganza">Maria Isabel of Braganza</a> (wife of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">Ferdinand VII of Spain</a>), as well as sometime candidates for the thrones of Poland and Greece, <a href="/wiki/Infante_Manuel,_Count_of_Our%C3%A9m" title="Infante Manuel, Count of Ourém">Infante Manuel, Count of Ourém</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Pedro, Duke of Braganza</a>, respectively, and numerous other notable figures in the histories of Europe and the Americas. The Braganzas were deposed from their thrones at the turn of the 19th-20th centuries, when <a href="/wiki/Pedro_II_of_Brazil" title="Pedro II of Brazil">Emperor Pedro II</a> was <a href="/wiki/Proclamation_of_the_Republic_(Brazil)" title="Proclamation of the Republic (Brazil)">deposed in Brazil</a>, in 1889, and when <a href="/wiki/Manuel_II_of_Portugal" title="Manuel II of Portugal">King Manuel II</a> was <a href="/wiki/5_October_1910_revolution" title="5 October 1910 revolution">deposed in Portugal</a>, in 1910.</p>
<p>Following the reign of King <a href="/wiki/John_VI_of_Portugal" title="John VI of Portugal">John VI of Portugal</a>, the Braganzas were split into three main branches of the family: the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Imperial_Family" title="Brazilian Imperial Family">Brazilian branch</a>, headed by King John VI's eldest son, Emperor <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Pedro I of Brazil</a>, the Constitutional branch, headed by Emperor Pedro I's eldest daughter, Queen <a href="/wiki/Maria_II_of_Portugal" title="Maria II of Portugal">Maria II of Portugal</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Miguelist" title="Miguelist">Miguelist branch</a>, headed by King John VI's second eldest son, King <a href="/wiki/Miguel_I_of_Portugal" title="Miguel I of Portugal">Miguel I of Portugal</a>. The Brazilian branch, following 1921, became the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Orl%C3%A9ans-Braganza" title="House of Orléans-Braganza">House of Orléans-Braganza</a>, whose leadership is disputed by two branches of its own: the Vassouras branch, headed by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Luiz_of_Orl%C3%A9ans-Braganza" title="Prince Luiz of Orléans-Braganza">Prince Luiz of Orléans-Braganza</a>, and the Petrópolis branch, headed by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Pedro_Carlos_of_Orl%C3%A9ans-Braganza" title="Prince Pedro Carlos of Orléans-Braganza">Prince Pedro Carlos of Orléans-Braganza</a>. The Constitutional branch died out with the death of King Manuel II in 1932, passing its claim to the Portuguese throne to the Miguelist Branch, by way of <a href="/wiki/Duarte_Nuno,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Duarte Nuno, Duke of Braganza">Duarte Nuno, Duke of Braganza</a>. The claim to the Portuguese Crown, and thus to the leadership of the House of Braganza, passed to Duarte Nuno's son, <a href="/wiki/Duarte_Pio,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Duarte Pio, Duke of Braganza">Duarte Pio, Duke of Braganza</a>, who is currently the most recognized pretender to the Portuguese throne.</p>
<p></p>

<h2>Contents</h2>
</div>
<ul>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>
<ul>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Feudal_establishment"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Feudal establishment</span></a></li>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Feudal_establishment">Feudal establishment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Feudal establishment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Afonso_first_Duke_of_Braganza.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1171" data-file-width="791" height="326" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Afonso_first_Duke_of_Braganza.jpg/220px-Afonso_first_Duke_of_Braganza.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Afonso_first_Duke_of_Braganza.jpg/330px-Afonso_first_Duke_of_Braganza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Afonso_first_Duke_of_Braganza.jpg/440px-Afonso_first_Duke_of_Braganza.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Afonso_first_Duke_of_Braganza.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Afonso_I,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Afonso I, Duke of Braganza">Afonso I</a>, first <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Braganza" title="Duke of Braganza">Duke of Braganza</a> and founder of the House of Braganza</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The House of Braganza originated with <a href="/wiki/Afonso_I,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Afonso I, Duke of Braganza">Afonso I</a>, an illegitimate son of King <a href="/wiki/John_I_of_Portugal" title="John I of Portugal">John I of Portugal</a>, founder of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Aviz" title="House of Aviz">House of Aviz</a>, and Inês Pires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-In.C3.AAs_Pires_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-In.C3.AAs_Pires-1">[a]</a></sup> Though Afonso was illegitimate, his father valued and cared for him a great deal, demonstrated by his arrangement of Afonso's marriage to <a href="/wiki/Beatriz_Pereira_de_Alvim" title="Beatriz Pereira de Alvim">Beatriz Pereira de Alvim</a>, daughter of <a href="/wiki/Nuno_%C3%81lvares_Pereira" title="Nuno Álvares Pereira">Nuno Álvares Pereira</a>, Portugal's most important general and a personal friend of King John I. As well as increasing his social status by his marriage into a well-established house, Afonso also became the eighth <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Barcelos" title="Count of Barcelos">Count of Barcelos</a>, an honour ceded to him by his father-in-law, who had been made the seventh count by John I.</p>
<p>With his newly consolidated place in the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_nobility" title="Portuguese nobility">nobility of Portugal</a>, Afonso commenced what would be a highly successful political and social career. In 1415 he took part in the <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Ceuta" title="Conquest of Ceuta">Conquest of Ceuta</a>, alongside his father, his brothers, and the leading members of the nobility and military. By the time of his father's death in 1433, Afonso had won favour with his brother, King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duarte_I_of_Portugal" title="Duarte I of Portugal">Duarte I</a> and the rest of high Portuguese society. With his brother's premature death in 1438, a regency was established for Afonso's nephew, the 6 year old King <a href="/wiki/Afonso_V_of_Portugal" title="Afonso V of Portugal">Afonso V</a>, under the leadership of the king's mother, <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_Aragon,_Queen_of_Portugal" title="Eleanor of Aragon, Queen of Portugal">Leonor of Aragon</a>, and later Afonso's brother, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infante_Pedro,_Duke_of_Coimbra" title="Infante Pedro, Duke of Coimbra">Infante Pedro, Duke of Coimbra</a>. The Duke of Coimbra's regency, however, soon proved unpopular and Afonso quickly became the King's preferred advisor. On 30 December 1442, the Duke of Coimbra, still the King's regent and thus acting in his name, created Afonso as the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Braganza" title="Duke of Braganza">Duke of Braganza</a>, as a gesture of good will and reconciliation between the two brothers. Afonso's elevation to the dukedom, the highest level of nobility, marked the foundation of the House of Braganza, which was to become a key family in Portuguese history.</p>
<p>As a result of the hard work and success of Afonso I, his children all secured successful positions and lived privileged lives. Afonso I's first son, <a href="/wiki/Afonso_of_Braganza,_1st_Marquis_of_Valen%C3%A7a" title="Afonso of Braganza, 1st Marquis of Valença">Afonso of Braganza</a>, was a prominent member of the nobility, having been ceded, by his grandfather, Nuno Álvares Pereira, the lucrative and powerful title of <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Our%C3%A9m" title="Count of Ourém">Count of Ourém</a>, in 1422. He was an accomplished diplomat, and served as the king's representative at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council_of_Basel" title="Council of Basel">Council of Basel</a> in 1436, and the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Florence" title="Council of Florence">Council of Florence</a> in 1439. In 1451, the Count of Ourém was made <a href="/wiki/Marquis_of_Valen%C3%A7a" title="Marquis of Valença">Marquis of Valença</a> and escorted <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_Portugal,_Holy_Roman_Empress" title="Eleanor of Portugal, Holy Roman Empress">Infanta Leonor of Portugal</a> to her husband <a href="/wiki/Frederick_III,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick III, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick III, Holy Roman Emperor</a>. Later, in 1458, he participated in the capture and conquest of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1cer-Ceguer" title="Alcácer-Ceguer">Alcácer-Ceguer</a>. The Marquis of Valença, however, died in 1460, one year before his father and therefore did not succeed him. Afonso I's first daughter, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabel_of_Braganza,_Lady_of_Reguengos_de_Monsaraz" title="Isabel of Braganza, Lady of Reguengos de Monsaraz">Isabel of Braganza</a>, married <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infante_Jo%C3%A3o,_Lord_of_Reguengos_de_Monsaraz" title="Infante João, Lord of Reguengos de Monsaraz">Infante João, Lord of Reguengos de Monsaraz</a>, thus relinking the House of Braganza to the Royal House of Portugal. Isabel's strategic marriage proved successful, and produced four children, whose descendants would be some of the most important in Iberian history. Afonso I's last child and successor, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_I,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Fernando I, Duke of Braganza">Fernando I, Duke of Braganza</a>, continued his legacy of prominence in the military and society.</p>
<p>When Fernando I was born, in 1403, his grandfather, Nuno Álvares Pereira, ceded him the title of <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Arraiolos" title="Count of Arraiolos">Count of Arraiolos</a>. Fernando became an accomplished military man, participating in various <a href="/wiki/Moroccan%E2%80%93Portuguese_conflicts" title="Moroccan–Portuguese conflicts">Portuguese imperial campaigns</a>. Though Fernando I was a popular and powerful member of the nobility, he did not always find himself in the favour of the king, most notably exemplified when Fernando I openly declaimed King Duarte I, at the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Cortes" title="Portuguese Cortes">Portuguese Cortes</a>, on the topic of the rescue and recovery of the King's brother, <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_the_Holy_Prince" title="Ferdinand the Holy Prince">Infante Fernando, Lord of Salvaterra de Magos</a> from the Moors. However, Fernando I became a favourite of both the royal and imperial government and of King Afonso V, earning him the position of Governor of Ceuta and the titles of <a href="/wiki/Marquis_of_Vila_Vi%C3%A7osa" title="Marquis of Vila Viçosa">Marquis of Vila Viçosa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Neiva" title="Count of Neiva">Count of Neiva</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fernando_II.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="422" data-file-width="336" height="276" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Fernando_II.png/220px-Fernando_II.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Fernando_II.png/330px-Fernando_II.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9a/Fernando_II.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fernando_II.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Fernando_II,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Fernando II, Duke of Braganza">Fernando II</a>, the duke whose <a href="/wiki/Fernando_II,_Duke_of_Braganza#Treason_and_Downfall" title="Fernando II, Duke of Braganza">supposed treason</a> had the House stripped and exiled</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Fernando I's children, by his wife, Joana de Castro, Lady of Cadaval, continued to enlarge the influence of the House of Braganza. Of his nine children, all six who survived to adulthood established themselves either through positions or marriages, though the actions of King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_II_of_Portugal" title="João II of Portugal">João II</a> would seek to weaken their influence. Fernando I's first son and successor, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_II,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Fernando II, Duke of Braganza">Fernando II</a>, was initially a bright and popular nobleman, but his conflict with King João II would see his and the House's downfall. His second son, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_of_Braganza,_1st_Marquis_of_Montemor-o-Novo" title="João of Braganza, 1st Marquis of Montemor-o-Novo">João of Braganza, 1st Marquis of Montemor-o-Novo</a>, was an accomplished military man and was made <a href="/wiki/Constable_of_Portugal" title="Constable of Portugal">Constable of Portugal</a>. Fernando's third son, Afonso of Braganza, became a popular nobleman of society and was made 1st <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Faro" title="Count of Faro">Count of Faro</a>. The Duke's fourth son, <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_of_Braganza" title="Álvaro of Braganza">Álvaro of Braganza</a>, inherited the fiefs of his mother, becoming the 5th Lord of Ferreira, 4th Lord of Cadaval, and 1st Lord of Tentúgal. Fernando's eldest surviving daughter, Beatriz of Braganza, married Pedro de Meneses, 1st <a href="/wiki/Marquis_of_Vila_Real" title="Marquis of Vila Real">Marquis of Vila Real</a>. Fernando's last surviving child, Guiomar of Braganza, married Henrique de Meneses, 4th <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Viana_do_Alentejo" title="Count of Viana do Alentejo">Count of Viana do Alentejo</a>. Ultimately, however, Fernando I's children and grandchildren would suffer great difficulty under the reign of King João II.</p>
<p>By the tenure of the third duke, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_II,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Fernando II, Duke of Braganza">Fernando II</a>, the House of Braganza was undoubtedly one of the greatest noble houses of Portugal and Iberia as a whole. Fernando II continued the House's legacy of acquisition and gained the title of <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Guimar%C3%A3es" title="Duke of Guimarães">Duke of Guimarães</a>. To the Duke and the House's downfall, however, King João II's reign concerned itself with the royal consolidation of power and the diminishment of the nobility. In his mission to centralize power, the King executed many nobleman of the great houses of Portugal, alongside confiscating their properties and exiling their families. Fernando II, having been a prominent and powerful nobleman, was accused of treason and executed by King João II; the House's titles and properties were merged into the crown and its members exiled to Castile.</p>
<p>Due to their father's misfortunes, Fernando II's children, from his marriage to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabella_of_Viseu" title="Isabella of Viseu">Isabel of Viseu</a>, daughter of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infante_Ferdinand,_Duke_of_Viseu" title="Infante Ferdinand, Duke of Viseu">Infante Fernando, Duke of Viseu and Beja</a>, initially had a tumultuous childhood; but King João II's successor, King <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">Manuel I</a>, who had previously himself been the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Beja" title="Duke of Beja">Duke of Beja</a>, chose to forgive the House and re-grant them all their properties in exchange for their loyalty. Fernando II's oldest surviving son and successor, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaime_I,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Jaime I, Duke of Braganza">Jaime I</a>, returned to Portugal and reestablished himself at <a href="/wiki/Vila_Vi%C3%A7osa" title="Vila Viçosa">Vila Viçosa</a>, the former seat of the Dukes. Fernando II's only other surviving son, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denis_of_Braganza,_Count_of_Lemos" title="Denis of Braganza, Count of Lemos">Dinis of Braganza</a>, married Beatriz de Castro Osório, Countess of Lemos, and had four children with her.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Princes_of_the_Renaissance">Princes of the Renaissance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Princes of the Renaissance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jaime_I_Braganca.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="492" data-file-width="480" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Jaime_I_Braganca.jpg/220px-Jaime_I_Braganca.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Jaime_I_Braganca.jpg/330px-Jaime_I_Braganca.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Jaime_I_Braganca.jpg/440px-Jaime_I_Braganca.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jaime_I_Braganca.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaime_I,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Jaime I, Duke of Braganza">Jaime I</a>, the Duke who restored the House's prestige after the <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal#Consolidation_of_power" title="John II of Portugal">João II affair</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Jaime I's tenure as Duke of Braganza was one of restoration and grandness. Upon his return to Portugal from exile, Jaime took possession of the House's formerly confiscated properties. In order to establish a new image for the House, he ordered the construction of a new seat for the House, which would become one of the largest palaces in Iberia, the <a href="/wiki/Ducal_Palace_of_Vila_Vi%C3%A7osa" title="Ducal Palace of Vila Viçosa">Ducal Palace of Vila Viçosa</a>. Jaime I's restoration also continued with the House's relations with the King, Jaime I having becoming a favourite of King Manuel I and even once his temporary heir. The Duke also had his share of scandal, having funded the conquest of the city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azamor" title="Azamor">Azamor</a>, for the royal crown as, as punishment for his ordering the murder of his first wife, Leonor Pérez de Guzman, daughter of <a href="/wiki/Juan_Alfonso_P%C3%A9rez_de_Guzm%C3%A1n,_3rd_Duke_of_Medina_Sidonia" title="Juan Alfonso Pérez de Guzmán, 3rd Duke of Medina Sidonia">Juan Alfonso Pérez de Guzmán, 3rd Duke of Medina Sidonia</a>.</p>
<p>The children of Jaime I, both the two first children by his first wife, Leonor of Pérez de Guzman, and the later eight children by his second wife, Joana of Mendoça, all saw successful lives under the restored House of Braganza. Jaime I's first daughter, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabella_of_Braganza,_Duchess_of_Guimar%C3%A3es" title="Isabella of Braganza, Duchess of Guimarães">Isabel of Braganza</a>, married <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infante_Edward,_4th_Duke_of_Guimar%C3%A3es" title="Infante Edward, 4th Duke of Guimarães">Infante Duarte, Duke of Guimarães</a>, and had three children, while his first son and successor, <a href="/wiki/Teod%C3%B3sio_I,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Teodósio I, Duke of Braganza">Teodósio I</a>, was a successful prince of the renaissance. Five of Jaime I's children, Jaime, Maria, Fulgêncio, Teotónio, and Vicência, all entered into religious orders. The Duke's second daughter, Joana of Braganza, married Bernardino de Cardenas, 3rd Marquis of Elche, and his third daughter, Eugénia of Braganza, married Francisco de Melo, 2nd <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marquis_of_Ferreira" title="Marquis of Ferreira">Marquis of Ferreira</a>. Jaime I's only other son, other than Teodósio I, to not enter into the church, <a href="/wiki/Constantino_of_Braganza" title="Constantino of Braganza">Constantino of Braganza</a>, married Maria de Melo, daughter of D. Rodrigo de Melo, 1st <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marquis_of_Ferreira" title="Marquis of Ferreira">Marquis of Ferreira</a>, but had no children. Constantino was famed as a great officer of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a>, having served as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_governors_of_Portuguese_India" title="List of governors of Portuguese India">Viceroy of Portuguese India</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_colonial_governors_of_Cape_Verde#Ribeira_Grande" title="List of colonial governors of Cape Verde">Captain of Ribeira Grande</a>, among other positions.</p>
<p>The fifth Duke, <a href="/wiki/Teod%C3%B3sio_I,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Teodósio I, Duke of Braganza">Teodósio I</a>, is remembered for being the personification of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Renaissance" title="Portuguese Renaissance">Portuguese Renaissance</a>. A patron of the arts and scholarly noble, Teodósio I maintained the prestige of the House of Braganza, although not leaving a significant mark on the House's history. The Duke notably ceded the Dukedom of Guimarães to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infante_Edward,_4th_Duke_of_Guimar%C3%A3es" title="Infante Edward, 4th Duke of Guimarães">Infante Duarte of Portugal</a> as the dowry of his sister, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabella_of_Braganza,_Duchess_of_Guimar%C3%A3es" title="Isabella of Braganza, Duchess of Guimarães">Isabel of Braganza</a>.</p>
<p>Teodósio I's first son, Jaime of Braganza, died before he could inherit his father's titles, fighting alongside King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sebastian_I_of_Portugal" title="Sebastian I of Portugal">Sebastião I</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Alc%C3%A1cer_Quibir" title="Battle of Alcácer Quibir">Battle of Alcácer Quibir</a>. The Duke's only daughter, Isabel of Braganza, married Miguel Luis de Meneses, 1st <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Caminha" title="Duke of Caminha">Duke of Caminha</a>, though their union had no issue. Teodósio I's last child and successor, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_I,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="João I, Duke of Braganza">João I</a>, lived a very different life from Teodósio I's calm and relatively peaceful tenure, having been involved in the controversies of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_succession_crisis_of_1580" title="Portuguese succession crisis of 1580">Portuguese succession crisis of 1580</a> and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Portuguese_Succession" title="War of the Portuguese Succession">War of the Portuguese Succession</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teod%C3%B3sio_I.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="495" data-file-width="480" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Teod%C3%B3sio_I.png/220px-Teod%C3%B3sio_I.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Teod%C3%B3sio_I.png/330px-Teod%C3%B3sio_I.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Teod%C3%B3sio_I.png/440px-Teod%C3%B3sio_I.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teod%C3%B3sio_I.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Teod%C3%B3sio_I,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Teodósio I, Duke of Braganza">Teodósio I</a>, the Duke who personified the prince of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Renaissance" title="Portuguese Renaissance">Portuguese Renaissance</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_I,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="João I, Duke of Braganza">João I</a>'s tenure as Duke was one intertwined with controversy and intrigue. Having been married to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catherine,_Duchess_of_Braganza" title="Catherine, Duchess of Braganza">Infanta Catarina</a>, daughter of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infante_Edward,_4th_Duke_of_Guimar%C3%A3es" title="Infante Edward, 4th Duke of Guimarães">Infante Duarte, Duke of Guimarães</a>, and thus a grandchild of King Manuel I, during the succession crisis of 1580, the couple pressed their claims to the Portuguese throne. Though Infanta Catarina was a popular claimant, her <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Dynasty" title="Philippine Dynasty">Habsburg</a> cousin was eventually crowned <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philip_I_of_Portugal" title="Philip I of Portugal">Philip I of Portugal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a> was established. In an attempt at reconciliation with the Brigantine House, King Philip I renewed the title of Constable of Portugal, which João I had held previously, to the Duke's first son, <a href="/wiki/Teod%C3%B3sio_II,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Teodósio II, Duke of Braganza">Teodósio II</a>, alongside other title and land grants to the Duke and the House.</p>
<p>João I's daughters, Maria, Serefina, Querubina, and Angélica, were some of the most eligible ladies of Portugal and all Iberia, though the only one to marry was Serefina of Braganza, who married Castilian <a href="/wiki/Juan_Fernandez_Pacheco,_5th_Duke_of_Escalona" title="Juan Fernandez Pacheco, 5th Duke of Escalona">Juan Fernandez Pacheco, 5th Duke of Escalona</a>. The Duke's oldest son and successor, Teodósio II, famously fought in the Battle of Alcácer Quibir at the age of ten and later became an accomplished general. João I's second son, Duarte of Braganza, was made 1st Marquis of Frechilla, and the Duke's third son, Alexandre of Braganza, became <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_%C3%89vora" title="Archbishop of Évora">Archbishop of Évora</a>, both receiving their titles and many concessions from King Philip I when the monarch was making amends with the House of Braganza. Unlike his other sons, João I's last son, Filipe of Braganza, died without marriage, children, or titles.</p>
<p>The seventh Duke, Teodósio II, became famous at a young age, having been made page to King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sebastian_I_of_Portugal" title="Sebastian I of Portugal">Sebastião I</a> and having marched into the Battle of Alcácer Quibir, alongside the King and his uncle, Jaime of Braganza, at the age of ten. Teodósio II later pledged his allegiance and became a faithful countryman to the Philippine Dynasty, having even defended <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> against King Philip I's rival claimant to the throne, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio,_Prior_of_Crato" title="António, Prior of Crato">António, Prior of Crato</a>, who had been acclaimed, by his supporters, as King António I of Portugal. In recognition for his military prowess, Teodósio II was made Constable of Portugal. The Duke's support and service to the Philippine Dynasty, earned the Braganzas more lands and titles and, by 1640, the House had amassed around 80,000 vassals, alongside numerous churches, orders, and institutions under its patronage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcMurdo1889363_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcMurdo1889363-2">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1603, Teodósio II married <a href="/wiki/Ana_de_Velasco_y_Gir%C3%B3n" title="Ana de Velasco y Girón">Ana de Velasco y Girón</a>, daughter of Castilian <a href="/wiki/Juan_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Velasco,_5th_Duke_of_Fr%C3%ADas" title="Juan Fernández de Velasco, 5th Duke of Frías">Juan Fernández de Velasco, 5th Duke of Frías</a>, and had four children with her. The Duke's first son and successor, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_IV_of_Portugal" title="João IV of Portugal">João II</a>, raise the House of Braganza to new heights of power, having launched the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Portuguese Restoration War</a> and been acclaimed King João IV of Portugal, thus installing the House as the ruling dynasty of Portugal. Teodósio II's second son, Duarte of Braganza, was made Lord of Vila do Conde and became a diplomat, serving at the court of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_III,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Ferdinand III, Holy Roman Emperor">Ferdinand III, Holy Roman Emperor</a>, but later died a prisoner as a cost of the Restoration War. Teodósio II's two other children, Alexandre and Catarina, both died without children, titles, or marriage.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Throne_of_Portugal">Throne of Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Throne of Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joao_IV.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1146" data-file-width="993" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Joao_IV.jpg/220px-Joao_IV.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Joao_IV.jpg/330px-Joao_IV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Joao_IV.jpg/440px-Joao_IV.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joao_IV.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_IV_of_Portugal" title="João IV of Portugal">João II</a> raised the noble house to the ruling dynasty as King João IV of Portugal.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Afonso_VI,_Rei_de_Portugal.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1287" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Afonso_VI%2C_Rei_de_Portugal.JPG/220px-Afonso_VI%2C_Rei_de_Portugal.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Afonso_VI%2C_Rei_de_Portugal.JPG/330px-Afonso_VI%2C_Rei_de_Portugal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Afonso_VI%2C_Rei_de_Portugal.JPG/440px-Afonso_VI%2C_Rei_de_Portugal.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Afonso_VI,_Rei_de_Portugal.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Afonso_VI_of_Portugal" title="Afonso VI of Portugal">Afonso VI of Portugal</a>, the king during whose reign the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Restoration War ended</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By 1640 the wise policies of D. Philip I in respect of Portugal were long past. The country was overtaxed, Portuguese colonies were left unprotected, and the King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philip_III_of_Portugal" title="Philip III of Portugal">Philip III of Portugal</a> no longer had the trust or support of most <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_nobility" title="Portuguese nobility">Portuguese nobility</a>. He was especially loathed by the powerful Portuguese guild of merchants. Portugal, like the rest of Philip's kingdoms, was on the verge of rebellion.</p>
<p>The eighth Duke of Braganza, D. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_IV_of_Portugal" title="João IV of Portugal">João II of Braganza</a>, had inherited the claim of his grandmother, Infanta Catarina of Portugal, and the remoter claim through of his grandfather João I of Braganza. Because of his claims, the discontent Portuguese nobility asked João II to lead their restoration as their king.</p>
<p>According to court historians, D. João II was a modest man without particular ambitions to the crown. Legend says that his wife, Dona <a href="/wiki/Luisa_de_Guzm%C3%A1n" title="Luisa de Guzmán">Luisa de Guzmán</a>, daughter of the duke of Medina-Sidonia, urged him to accept the offer, saying "I'd rather be queen for one day than duchess for a lifetime." He accepted the leadership of the rebellion, which was successful, and was acclaimed João IV of Portugal on 1 December 1640.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width: 220px;">
<div style="width: 220px; height: 220px; overflow: hidden;">
<div style="position: relative; top: -3px; left: -222px; width: 445px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portugal_1729_8_Escudos.jpg"><img alt="Braganza coat of arms on the reverse of a 1729 eight gold escudo coin (depicting João V on the front)." data-file-height="2264" data-file-width="4444" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Portugal_1729_8_Escudos.jpg/445px-Portugal_1729_8_Escudos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Portugal_1729_8_Escudos.jpg/668px-Portugal_1729_8_Escudos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Portugal_1729_8_Escudos.jpg/890px-Portugal_1729_8_Escudos.jpg 2x" width="445"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portugal_1729_8_Escudos.jpg" title="File:Portugal 1729 8 Escudos.jpg">File:Portugal 1729 8 Escudos.jpg</a></div>
Braganza coat of arms on the reverse of a 1729 eight gold <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_escudo" title="Portuguese escudo">escudo</a> coin (depicting <a href="/wiki/John_V_of_Portugal" title="John V of Portugal">João V</a> on the front).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the accession of the Braganzas to the throne, the duchy was linked to the Crown. "Duke of Braganza" became the traditional title of the heir to the throne, together with <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Brazil" title="Prince of Brazil">Prince of Brazil</a> and, later, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Royal_of_Portugal" title="Prince Royal of Portugal">Prince Royal of Portugal</a>, much as <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales" title="Prince of Wales">Prince of Wales</a> is in the United Kingdom or <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Asturias" title="Prince of Asturias">Prince of Asturias</a> in Spain.</p>
<p>Under D. João's sons D. <a href="/wiki/Afonso_VI_of_Portugal" title="Afonso VI of Portugal">Afonso VI</a> and D. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pedro_II_of_Portugal" title="Pedro II of Portugal">Pedro II</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese colonial empire</a>, part of which was lost during the Spanish occupation, was restored and expanded, bringing new wealth to Portugal.</p>
<p>The zenith of the Braganza dynasty came with the long reign of D. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_V_of_Portugal" title="João V of Portugal">João V</a> (1706–1750), who ruled with grandeur and piety. The reign of D. <a href="/wiki/Joseph_I_of_Portugal" title="Joseph I of Portugal">José I</a>, son of D. João V, was marked by the <a href="/wiki/1755_Lisbon_earthquake" title="1755 Lisbon earthquake">great earthquake</a>, which struck <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> in 1755. The political genius of his reign was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A3o_Jos%C3%A9_de_Carvalho_e_Melo,_1st_Marquess_of_Pombal" title="Sebastião José de Carvalho e Melo, 1st Marquess of Pombal">1st Marquis of Pombal</a>. The end of the 18th century was characterized by stability, under the rule of Dona <a href="/wiki/Maria_I_of_Portugal" title="Maria I of Portugal">Maria I</a> (1777–1816), who discharged Pombal at her accession. Unfortunately Dona Maria became psychologically unstable, displaying similar symptoms to <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George III of the United Kingdom">George III of the United Kingdom</a> in his later years.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Realm_in_Brazil">Realm in Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Realm in Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1808, faced with impending <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Napoleonic invasion</a>, the Braganzas <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_the_Portuguese_Court_to_Brazil" title="Transfer of the Portuguese Court to Brazil">transferred their royal court</a> to the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Brazil" title="State of Brazil">State of Brazil</a>, Portugal's largest colony. Some time after they had crossed the Atlantic, a royal decree changed the status of Brazil from a Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colony</a> into kingdom alongside Portugal, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil_and_the_Algarves" title="United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves">United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves</a> was formed. In 1821, D. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_VI_of_Portugal" title="João VI of Portugal">João VI</a>, who succeeded in 1816, returned to Portugal.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Retrato_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_(1802)_-_Domingos_Sequeira_(Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Ajuda).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="741" height="304" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Retrato_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_%281802%29_-_Domingos_Sequeira_%28Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Ajuda%29.png/220px-Retrato_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_%281802%29_-_Domingos_Sequeira_%28Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Ajuda%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Retrato_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_%281802%29_-_Domingos_Sequeira_%28Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Ajuda%29.png/330px-Retrato_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_%281802%29_-_Domingos_Sequeira_%28Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Ajuda%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Retrato_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_%281802%29_-_Domingos_Sequeira_%28Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Ajuda%29.png/440px-Retrato_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_%281802%29_-_Domingos_Sequeira_%28Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Ajuda%29.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Retrato_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_(1802)_-_Domingos_Sequeira_(Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Ajuda).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_VI_of_Portugal" title="João VI of Portugal">João VI of Portugal</a>'s children split the Brigantine House into three branches.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>D. <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Pedro, Prince Royal of Portugal, Brazil, and the Algarves</a>, the eldest son of D. João VI and also regent in Brazil, sided with the Brazilian rebels in January 1822. He <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_independence" title="Brazilian independence">was acclaimed</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Brazil" title="Emperor of Brazil">Emperor D. Pedro I</a> of an independent Brazil in 1822, founding the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a>. D. Pedro I ruled Brazil until 1831, when he abdicated in favor of his young son D. <a href="/wiki/Pedro_II_of_Brazil" title="Pedro II of Brazil">Pedro II</a>, and returned to Portugal to aid his daughter D. Maria II (see below).</p>
<p>D. Pedro II, being only 6 years old at the time of his coronation, had a regency established. The regency would rule until 1840, when the Emperor turned 14 years old. His reign would last until 1889, when the Brazilian monarchy was abolished. His reign would see the <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Brazil" title="Slavery in Brazil">abolition of slavery</a> in Brazil, economic growth, and very long periods of tranquility and development in his empire.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Warring_branches">Warring branches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Warring branches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Portugal, D. Pedro I of Brazil became King as D. Pedro IV (1826), but no one wanted to re-establish the union of Portugal and Brazil. Pedro abdicated the Portuguese throne in favor of his daughter Princess <a href="/wiki/Maria_II_of_Portugal" title="Maria II of Portugal">Maria da Glória</a>, then seven years old. D. Pedro's brother D. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miguel_of_Portugal" title="Miguel of Portugal">Miguel</a> was to act as Regent, and to marry Maria when she came of age. In 1828, Miguel instead proclaimed himself King of Portugal and repudiated the liberal constitution granted by D. João VI, trying to establish an <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a>.</p>
<p>In 1828, Maria II was forced into exile by her uncle, the new King Miguel I. Her father D. Pedro IV of Portugal returned from Brazil, launched a successful military campaign, from the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, against Miguel I. He finally defeated and exiled Miguel I in 1834. Though exiled, Miguel would not give up his claim to the throne and would establish the <b><a href="/wiki/Miguelist#The_Miguelist_branch_of_the_Braganzas" title="Miguelist">Miguelist branch</a></b> of the House of Braganza. The strategic marriages of his children to the various royal houses of Europe would earn him the nickname the "Grandfather of Europe" (<i>see <a href="/wiki/Descendants_of_Miguel_I_of_Portugal" title="Descendants of Miguel I of Portugal">Descendants of Miguel I of Portugal</a></i>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Peace_in_Portugal">Peace in Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Peace in Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SMF_Manoel_II.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="604" data-file-width="415" height="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/SMF_Manoel_II.jpg/220px-SMF_Manoel_II.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/SMF_Manoel_II.jpg/330px-SMF_Manoel_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9a/SMF_Manoel_II.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SMF_Manoel_II.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Manuel_II_of_Portugal" title="Manuel II of Portugal">Manuel II</a>, the last King of Portugal and the last Braganza monarch.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Maria II married <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Portugal" title="Ferdinand II of Portugal">Prince Ferdinand of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha</a>. Maria II was succeeded in 1853 by her son D. <a href="/wiki/Pedro_V_of_Portugal" title="Pedro V of Portugal">Pedro V</a>, a hard-working reformer who died prematurely in 1861 due to cholera. D. Pedro V was succeeded by his brother D. <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_I_of_Portugal" title="Luís I of Portugal">Luís</a>, as D. Pedro V had no children.</p>
<p>D. Luís I was succeeded in 1889 by his son D. <a href="/wiki/Carlos_I_of_Portugal" title="Carlos I of Portugal">Carlos</a>. Carlos was <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Regicide" title="Lisbon Regicide">assassinated in 1908 together with his eldest son</a>, D. <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Filipe,_Prince_Royal_of_Portugal" title="Luís Filipe, Prince Royal of Portugal">Luís Filipe, Prince Royal of Portugal and Duke of Braganza</a>, by republicans. His younger son, D. <a href="/wiki/Manuel_II_of_Portugal" title="Manuel II of Portugal">Manuel, Duke of Beja</a>, survived the attack on his father and elder brother and became King as Manuel II, but was toppled two years later in the <a href="/wiki/5_October_1910_revolution" title="5 October 1910 revolution">1910 republican revolution</a>. After the revolution, Manuel was forced into exile in England by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_First_Republic" title="Portuguese First Republic">Portuguese First Republic</a>, but he would continue to support his <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">fatherland</a> until his death.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_Brazil">Imperial Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Imperial Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ant%C3%B4nio_Joaquim_Franco_Velasco_-_Dom_Pedro_I,_Imperador_do_Brasil.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="374" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Ant%C3%B4nio_Joaquim_Franco_Velasco_-_Dom_Pedro_I%2C_Imperador_do_Brasil.jpg/220px-Ant%C3%B4nio_Joaquim_Franco_Velasco_-_Dom_Pedro_I%2C_Imperador_do_Brasil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Ant%C3%B4nio_Joaquim_Franco_Velasco_-_Dom_Pedro_I%2C_Imperador_do_Brasil.jpg/330px-Ant%C3%B4nio_Joaquim_Franco_Velasco_-_Dom_Pedro_I%2C_Imperador_do_Brasil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4d/Ant%C3%B4nio_Joaquim_Franco_Velasco_-_Dom_Pedro_I%2C_Imperador_do_Brasil.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ant%C3%B4nio_Joaquim_Franco_Velasco_-_Dom_Pedro_I,_Imperador_do_Brasil.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Pedro I</a>, the first monarch of the independent Brazil.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pedro_II_Admiral_Brazil_1870.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2820" data-file-width="2029" height="306" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Pedro_II_Admiral_Brazil_1870.jpg/220px-Pedro_II_Admiral_Brazil_1870.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Pedro_II_Admiral_Brazil_1870.jpg/330px-Pedro_II_Admiral_Brazil_1870.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Pedro_II_Admiral_Brazil_1870.jpg/440px-Pedro_II_Admiral_Brazil_1870.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pedro_II_Admiral_Brazil_1870.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Pedro_II_of_Brazil" title="Pedro II of Brazil">Pedro II</a>, the last Emperor of Brazil.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 7 September 1822, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Dom Pedro of Braganza, Prince Royal of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves</a>, member of the House of Braganza, heir apparent to the Portuguese throne and Regent of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Brazil" title="Kingdom of Brazil">Kingdom of Brazil</a>, declared the country's independence from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil_and_the_Algarves" title="United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves">United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves</a> and was acclaimed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Brazil" title="Emperor of Brazil">Emperor of Brazil</a>. On 12 October, the prince was acclaimed Pedro I, first Emperor of the newly created Empire of Brazil, a constitutional monarchy. In 1825, signing the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rio_de_Janeiro_(1825)" title="Treaty of Rio de Janeiro (1825)">treaty of Rio de Janeiro</a> of this date, his father, King Dom <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_VI_of_Portugal" title="João VI of Portugal">João VI</a>, recognized the independence of the new state, the former Portuguese dominion, now <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a>.</p>
<p>Pedro I encountered a number of crises during his reign. A secessionist rebellion in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cisplatine_Province" title="Cisplatine Province">Cisplatine Province</a> in early 1825 and the subsequent attempt by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_the_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" title="United Provinces of the Río de la Plata">United Provinces of the Río de la Plata</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>) to annex Cisplatina led the Empire into the failed <a href="/wiki/Cisplatine_War" title="Cisplatine War">Cisplatine War</a>. In March 1826, João VI died and Pedro I inherited the Portuguese crown, briefly becoming King Pedro IV of Portugal before abdicating in favor of his eldest daughter, <a href="/wiki/Maria_II_of_Portugal" title="Maria II of Portugal">Maria II</a>. The situation worsened in 1828 when the war in the south ended with Brazil's loss of Cisplatina, which would become the independent republic of <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>. During the same year in Lisbon, Maria II's throne was usurped by <a href="/wiki/Miguel_I_of_Portugal" title="Miguel I of Portugal">Prince Miguel</a>, Pedro I's younger brother.</p>
<p>Other difficulties arose when the Empire's parliament opened in 1826. Pedro I, along with a significant percentage of the legislature, argued for an independent judiciary, a popularly elected legislature and a government which would be led by the emperor who held broad executive powers and prerogatives. Others in parliament argued for a similar structure, only with a less influential role for the monarch and the legislative branch being dominant in policy and governance. The struggle over whether the government would be dominated by the emperor or by the parliament was carried over into debates from 1826 to 1831 on the establishment of the governmental and political structure. Unable to deal with the problems in both Brazil and Portugal simultaneously, the Emperor abdicated on behalf of his son, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_II_of_Brazil" title="Pedro II of Brazil">Pedro II</a>, on 7 April 1831 and immediately sailed for Europe to <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Wars" title="Liberal Wars">restore his daughter to her throne</a>.</p>
<p>Pedro I's successor in Brazil was his five-year-old son, Pedro II. As the latter was still a minor, a weak regency was created. The power vacuum resulting from the absence of a ruling monarch as the ultimate arbiter in political disputes led to regional civil wars between local factions. Having inherited an empire on the verge of disintegration, Pedro II, once he was declared of age in 1840, with 14 years old, managed to bring peace and stability to the country, which eventually became an emerging international power. Brazil was victorious in three international conflicts (the <a href="/wiki/Platine_War" title="Platine War">Platine War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Uruguayan_War" title="Uruguayan War">Uruguayan War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a>) under Pedro II's rule, and the Empire prevailed in several other international disputes and outbreaks of domestic strife. With prosperity and economic development came an influx of European immigration, including Protestants and Jews, although Brazil remained mostly Catholic. Slavery, which had initially been widespread, was restricted by successive legislation until its final abolition in 1888 by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabel_of_Brazil" title="Isabel of Brazil">Princess Isabel</a>.</p>
<p>Even though the last four decades of Pedro II's reign were marked by continuous internal peace and economic prosperity, he had no desire to see the monarchy survive beyond his lifetime and made no effort to maintain support for the institution. The next in line to the throne was his daughter Isabel, but neither Pedro II nor the ruling classes considered a female monarch acceptable. Lacking any viable heir, the Empire's political leaders saw no reason to defend the monarchy. Although there was no desire among the majority of Brazilians to change the country's form of government, republicans began pressuring army officers to overthrow the monarchy. After a 58-year reign, on 15 November 1889 the Emperor was overthrown in a sudden <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> led by a clique of military leaders whose goal was the formation of a republic headed by a dictator, forming the <a href="/wiki/First_Brazilian_Republic" title="First Brazilian Republic">First Brazilian Republic</a>. Throughout the coup Pedro II showed no emotion, as if unconcerned about the outcome. He dismissed all suggestions put forward by politicians and military leaders for quelling the rebellion. The Emperor and his family were sent into exile in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. Although there was significant monarchist reaction after the fall of the Empire, this was thoroughly suppressed, and neither Pedro II nor his daughter and heiress supported a forced restoration.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_Braganzas">Modern Braganzas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Modern Braganzas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_Braganzas">Portuguese Braganzas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Portuguese Braganzas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jantar_dos_Conjurados.2008_029_(crop).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1996" data-file-width="1292" height="340" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Jantar_dos_Conjurados.2008_029_%28crop%29.jpg/220px-Jantar_dos_Conjurados.2008_029_%28crop%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Jantar_dos_Conjurados.2008_029_%28crop%29.jpg/330px-Jantar_dos_Conjurados.2008_029_%28crop%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Jantar_dos_Conjurados.2008_029_%28crop%29.jpg/440px-Jantar_dos_Conjurados.2008_029_%28crop%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jantar_dos_Conjurados.2008_029_(crop).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Duarte_Pio,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Duarte Pio, Duke of Braganza">Duarte Pio, Duke of Braganza</a>, head of the House of Braganza and principal pretender to the Portuguese throne since 1976.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1835, Queen Maria II of Portugal married Prince Ferdinand of Saxe-Coburg-Gotha, later King <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Portugal" title="Ferdinand II of Portugal">Ferdinand II of Portugal</a>. Despite the tradition of following the custom of patrilineal descent of royal houses, common throughout Europe, the children of the marriage between Queen Maria II and King Fernando II were members of the House of Braganza and ruled Portugal as Brigantine monarchs, not as Saxe-Coburg-Gotha monarchs. Some foreign genealogists have classified the descendants of Maria II and Fernando II into a separate house, usually named the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Braganza-Saxe-Coburg_and_Gotha" title="House of Braganza-Saxe-Coburg and Gotha">House of Braganza-Saxe-Coburg and Gotha</a> however, Article 5 of the Portuguese constitution of 1826 clearly states that "<i>Continues the Reigning Dynasty of the Most Serene House of Braganza in the Person of Lady Princess Maria da Glória, by the Abdication and Cession of Her August Father Lord Pedro I, Emperor of Brazil, Legitimate Heir and Successor of Lord João VI.</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the revolution of 1910, King D. Manuel II settled in England until his death in 1932. He was childless, and descendants of D. Miguel (the usurper of 1826) claimed the throne. In 1920–22, the two (of the now four) branches of the House of Braganza negotiated a pact under which D. Manuel named as his heir D. <a href="/wiki/Duarte_Nuno,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Duarte Nuno, Duke of Braganza">Duarte Nuno of Braganza</a>, grandson of D. Miguel. D. Duarte Nuno, now Duke of Braganza, remained the Braganza pretender until his death in 1976. In 1942, he married a great-granddaughter of Emperor D. Pedro II of Brazil, uniting the two lines of the House.</p>
<p>In 1950 Portugal repealed the law of exile against the Braganzas, and D. Duarte Nuno moved to the country in 1952.</p>
<p>Dom Duarte Nuno was succeeded as pretender by his son, D. <a href="/wiki/Duarte_Pio,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Duarte Pio, Duke of Braganza">Duarte Pio of Braganza</a> (born 1945). D. Duarte Pio served in the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Armed_Forces" title="Portuguese Armed Forces">Portuguese Armed Forces</a> and took the customary oath of allegiance to the Republic, but Portuguese monarchists still recognize him as the pretender to the Portuguese throne. In 1995 he married Dona <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabel_de_Her%C3%A9dia" title="Isabel de Herédia">Isabel de Herédia</a>, a Portuguese businesswoman and descendent of the Viscount of Ribeira Brava. He worked actively in support of the independence of <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a> from <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>.</p>
<p>Duarte Pio and Isabel have three children, each bearing the traditional stylings of the Braganzas. Duarte Pio's oldest son is <a href="/wiki/Afonso,_Prince_of_Beira" title="Afonso, Prince of Beira">Afonso de Santa Maria</a>, who bears the traditional titles of <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Beira" title="Prince of Beira">Prince of Beira</a> (as heir apparent to the heir apparent to the King of Portugal) and <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Barcelos" title="Duke of Barcelos">Duke of Barcelos</a> (as heir apparent to the Duke of Braganza). He has a brother, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dinis,_Duke_of_Porto" title="Dinis, Duke of Porto">Dinis, Duke of Porto</a>, and a sister, <a href="/wiki/Infanta_Maria_Francisca_of_Portugal_(b._1997)" title="Infanta Maria Francisca of Portugal (b. 1997)">Infanta Maria Francisca</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Maria_Pia_de_Saxe-Coburgo_e_Bragan%C3%A7a" title="Maria Pia de Saxe-Coburgo e Bragança">Maria Pia de Saxe-Coburgo e Bragança</a>, who claimed she was an illegitimate daughter of King D. Carlos I of Portugal, began asserting that she was the heir to the throne from 1957. Allegedly, she adopted the Italian Rosario Poidimani, transferring her claimed rights to the Portuguese throne to him.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazilian_Braganzas">Brazilian Braganzas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Brazilian Braganzas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Domluis.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="404" data-file-width="280" height="317" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/69/Domluis.jpg/220px-Domluis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/69/Domluis.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Domluis.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Prince_Luiz_of_Orl%C3%A9ans-Braganza" title="Prince Luiz of Orléans-Braganza">Prince Luiz of Orléans-Braganza</a>, Head of the Brazilian Imperial House and <i>de jure</i> Emperor of Brazil since 1981.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the military coup of 1889, Emperor D. Pedro II settled in France until his death in 1891. His eldest daughter and family goes to live in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chateau_d%27Eu" title="Chateau d'Eu">Chateau d'Eu</a> in french <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a>. She was recognized by the very brazilian monarchists as Empress-in-Exile as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabel_of_Brazil" title="Isabel of Brazil">D. Isabel I of Brazil</a>, until her death in 1921. She was succeded by her grandson, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Pedro_Henrique_of_Orl%C3%A9ans-Braganza" title="Prince Pedro Henrique of Orléans-Braganza">Prince Pedro Henrique of Orléans-Braganza</a>, as <a href="/wiki/House_of_Orl%C3%A9ans-Braganza" title="House of Orléans-Braganza">Head of the Imperial House of Brazil</a>, and he by his son and current Head, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Luiz_of_Orl%C3%A9ans-Braganza" title="Prince Luiz of Orléans-Braganza">Prince Luiz of Orléans-Braganza</a>.</p>
<p>With the fall of the banishment of the Imperial Family in 1920, some Princes returned to live in the fatherland, while another remains in Europe. After the end of the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Prince Pedro Henrique, then Head of the Imperial House and married to <a href="/wiki/Princess_Maria_Elisabeth_of_Bavaria" title="Princess Maria Elisabeth of Bavaria">Princess Maria Elisabeth of Bavaria</a>, finally came to Brazil with his big family, althrought the Imperial House of Brazil was divided in two branches because of the rennounce of <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Alc%C3%A2ntara,_Prince_of_Gr%C3%A3o-Par%C3%A1" title="Pedro de Alcântara, Prince of Grão-Pará">Pedro de Alcântara, Prince of Grão-Pará</a> in 1908.</p>
<p>Today, some members of the two branches of the Imperial Family live in the <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Gr%C3%A3o-Par%C3%A1" title="Palácio do Grão-Pará">Grão-Pará Palace</a>, some married to european royals and nobles live in Europe, and the most live like commom people in their houses or apartments. Very active, the Vassouras Branch of the Imperial Family, most recognized nationally and internationally, led a growing movement to the restoration across the brazilian biggest streets.</p>

<td><a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Braganza" title="Duke of Braganza">Duke of Braganza</a>; <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Guimar%C3%A3es" title="Duke of Guimarães">Duke of Guimarães</a>;<br/>
first Braganza <a href="/wiki/List_of_Portuguese_monarchs" title="List of Portuguese monarchs">monarch of Portugal</a></td>
</tr>
</table>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Genealogy">Genealogy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Genealogy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Genealogical_tree_of_the_monarchs_of_Portugal" title="Genealogical tree of the monarchs of Portugal">Genealogical tree of the monarchs of Portugal</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ducal_line:_Afonso_I_to_Teod.C3.B3sio_II_.281377-1630.29">Ducal line: Afonso I to Teodósio II (1377-1630)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ducal line: Afonso I to Teodósio II (1377-1630)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<small><a href="/wiki/List_of_Portuguese_monarchs" title="List of Portuguese monarchs">King of Portugal and the Algarves</a><br/>
8th <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Braganza" title="Duke of Braganza">Duke of Braganza</a><small><br/>
(1604-1656)<br/>
<a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heraldic_Royal_Crown_of_Portugal_-_Four_Arches.svg"><img alt="Heraldic Royal Crown of Portugal - Four Arches.svg" data-file-height="199" data-file-width="300" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Heraldic_Royal_Crown_of_Portugal_-_Four_Arches.svg/30px-Heraldic_Royal_Crown_of_Portugal_-_Four_Arches.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Heraldic_Royal_Crown_of_Portugal_-_Four_Arches.svg/45px-Heraldic_Royal_Crown_of_Portugal_-_Four_Arches.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Heraldic_Royal_Crown_of_Portugal_-_Four_Arches.svg/60px-Heraldic_Royal_Crown_of_Portugal_-_Four_Arches.svg.png 2x" width="30"/></a><br/>
<a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shield_of_the_Kingdom_of_Portugal_(1481-1910).png"><img alt="Shield of the Kingdom of Portugal (1481-1910).png" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="300" height="36" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Shield_of_the_Kingdom_of_Portugal_%281481-1910%29.png/30px-Shield_of_the_Kingdom_of_Portugal_%281481-1910%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Shield_of_the_Kingdom_of_Portugal_%281481-1910%29.png/45px-Shield_of_the_Kingdom_of_Portugal_%281481-1910%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Shield_of_the_Kingdom_of_Portugal_%281481-1910%29.png/60px-Shield_of_the_Kingdom_of_Portugal_%281481-1910%29.png 2x" width="30"/></a></small></small></td>
<td colspan="2" rowspan="2">
<div style="width:2em;height:2em"><span style="font:1px/1px serif"> </span></div>
</td>
<td colspan="6" rowspan="2" style="border: 2px solid black; padding: 0.2em; ; background-color: #F0F8FF"><b><small>From him descend<br/>
the lines of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dukes_of_Fr%C3%ADas" title="Dukes of Frías">Dukes<br/>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_line:_Jo.C3.A3o_IV_to_Jo.C3.A3o_VI_.281604-1826.29">Royal line: João IV to João VI (1604-1826)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Royal line: João IV to João VI (1604-1826)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Genealogical tree of the House of Braganza, from its first monarch, <a href="/wiki/John_IV_of_Portugal" title="John IV of Portugal">João IV, King of Portugal</a>, to the fracture of the house into its three main branches, in the issue of <a href="/wiki/John_IV_of_Portugal" title="John IV of Portugal">João VI, King of United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil, and the Algarves</a>:</p>
<table style="border-spacing: 0; font-size:80%" title="Braganza">
<tr style="height: 1px; text-align: center;">
<td colspan="2" rowspan="2">
<div style="width:2em;height:2em"><span style="font:1px/1px serif"> </span></div>
</td>
<td colspan="2" rowspan="2">
<div style="width:2em;height:2em"><span style="font:1px/1px serif"> </span></div>
</td>
<td colspan="2" rowspan="2">
<div style="width:2em;height:2em"><span style="font:1px/1px serif"> </span></div>
</td>
<td colspan="2" rowspan="2">
<div style="width:2em;height:2em"><span style="font:1px/1px serif"> </span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sceptre_of_the_Carta_Constituicional.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="358" height="313" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Sceptre_of_the_Carta_Constituicional.jpg/140px-Sceptre_of_the_Carta_Constituicional.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Sceptre_of_the_Carta_Constituicional.jpg/210px-Sceptre_of_the_Carta_Constituicional.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Sceptre_of_the_Carta_Constituicional.jpg/280px-Sceptre_of_the_Carta_Constituicional.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sceptre_of_the_Carta_Constituicional.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Sceptre_of_the_Dragon" title="Sceptre of the Dragon">Sceptre of the Dragon</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wyvern">Wyvern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Wyvern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The traditional symbol and <a href="/wiki/Crest_(heraldry)" title="Crest (heraldry)">crest</a> of the House of Braganza is a green <a href="/wiki/Wyvern" title="Wyvern">wyvern</a>, commonly taken to be a <a href="/wiki/Dragon" title="Dragon">dragon</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barbosa_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barbosa-10">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[5]</a></sup> representing <a href="/wiki/Saint_George" title="Saint George">Saint George</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[6]</a></sup> patron saint of Portugal. This symbol can be found in many different monuments in Portugal and Brazil, such as the <a href="/wiki/Monument_to_the_Independence_of_Brazil" title="Monument to the Independence of Brazil">Monument to the Independence of Brazil</a> in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a> and in the palaces of the Imperial family in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Museum_of_Brazil" title="Imperial Museum of Brazil">Petrópolis</a>. It is famously found atop the Portuguese Crown Sceptre, the <a href="/wiki/Sceptre_of_the_Dragon" title="Sceptre of the Dragon">Sceptre of the Dragon</a> and the Sceptre of the Emperor of Brazil. The wyvern is also sometimes used as a <a href="/wiki/Supporter" title="Supporter">supporter</a> in the coat of arms of both the Brazilian and Portuguese branches of the family. Because of its use in heraldry by the Braganza as the ruling house, and given Pedro IV's link with <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>, a dragon was added to the old coat of arms of the municipality of Porto<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barbosa_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barbosa-10">[3]</a></sup> and is still a part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F.C._Porto" title="F.C. Porto">F.C. Porto</a>'s coat of arms, who are nicknamed "the dragons".</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Endnotes">Endnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Braganza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Endnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-In.C3.AAs_Pires-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-In.C3.AAs_Pires_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There is some controversy regarding the ancestry of Inês Pires (born in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Borba_(Portugal)" title="Borba (Portugal)">Borba</a>, c. 1350). She was the daughter of <i>Pedro Esteves</i> (for that she is sometimes called <i>Inês Pires Esteves</i>) and <i>Maria Anes</i> ("Grande Enciclopédia Portuguesa e Brasileira", Editorial Enciclopédia, Lisboa, vol. 4, pp. 172; António Caetano de Sousa, "História Genealógica da Casa Real Portuguesa", Atlântida Ed., Coimbra, 1946, vol. 2, pp. 25). Some historians and genealogist claim that her father was a <i><a href="/wiki/Converso" title="Converso">converso</a></i> - a Jew converted to Catholicism (Augusto Soares d' Azevedo Barbosa de Pinho Leal, "Portugal Antigo e Moderno", Cota d' Armas, Lisboa, 1990; Isabel Violante Pereira, "De Mendo da Guarda a D. Manuel I", Livros Horizonte, Lisboa, 2001), while the majority of sources give her a long and well attested noble Christian ancestry (Felgueiras Gayo, "Nobiliário das Famílias de Portugal", Carvalhos de Basto, Braga, 1989).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Duarte_Pio-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Duarte_Pio_4-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Duarte_Pio_4-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Title currently held by <a href="/wiki/Duarte_Pio,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Duarte Pio, Duke of Braganza">Duarte Pio, Duke of Braganza</a></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Afonso_de_Santa_Maria-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Afonso_de_Santa_Maria_5-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Title currently held by <a href="/wiki/Afonso,_Prince_of_Beira" title="Afonso, Prince of Beira">Afonso, Prince of Beira</a></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Afonso_de_Santa_Maria_e_Duarte_Pio-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Afonso_de_Santa_Maria_e_Duarte_Pio_6-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Titles currently held by <a href="/wiki/Duarte_Pio,_Duke_of_Braganza" title="Duarte Pio, Duke of Braganza">Duarte Pio, Duke of Braganza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afonso,_Prince_of_Beira" title="Afonso, Prince of Beira">Afonso, Prince of Beira</a></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Dinis-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Dinis_7-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Title currently held <a href="/wiki/Infante_Dinis,_Duke_of_Porto" title="Infante Dinis, Duke of Porto">Infante Dinis, Duke of Porto</a></span></li>
